**File:** `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/app/api/teams/[id]/route.ts`  

**Old:**  
```
export async function GET(
  request: NextRequest,
  { params }: { params: Promise<{ id: string }> }
) {
  const { id } = await params
  const team = getTeam(id)
  if (!team) {
    return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Team not found' }, { status: 404 })
  }
  const agentId = request.headers.get('X-Agent-Id') || undefined
  const access = checkTeamAccess({ teamId: id, requestingAgentId: agentId })
  if (!access.allowed) {
    return NextResponse.json({ error: access.reason }, { status: 403 })
  }
  return NextResponse.json({ team })
}
```

**New:**  
```
export async function GET(
  request: NextRequest,
  { params }: { params: Promise<{ id: string }> }
) {
  try {
    const { id } = await params
    const team = getTeam(id)
    if (!team) {
      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Team not found' }, { status: 404 })
    }
    const agentId = request.headers.get('X-Agent-Id') || undefined
    const access = checkTeamAccess({ teamId: id, requestingAgentId: agentId })
    if (!access.allowed) {
      return NextResponse.json({ error: access.reason }, { status: 403 })
    }
    return NextResponse.json({ team })
  } catch (error) {
    console.error('[teams] GET error:', error)
    return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Internal server error' }, { status: 500 })
  }
}
```

**Result:**

export async function DELETE(
  request: NextRequest,
  { params }: { params: Promise<{ id: string }> }
) {
  const { id } = await params
  const agentId = request.headers.get('X-Agent-Id') || undefined
  const access = checkTeamAccess({ teamId: id, requestingAgentId: agentId })
  if (!access.allowed) {
    return NextResponse.json({ error: access.reason }, { status: 403 })
  }
  const deleted = await deleteTeam(id)
  if (!deleted) {
    return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Team not found' }, { status: 404 })
  }
  return NextResponse.json({ success: true })
}
```

**New:**  
```
export async function DELETE(
  request: NextRequest,
  { params }: { params: Promise<{ id: string }> }
) {
  try {
    const { id } = await params
    const agentId = request.headers.get('X-Agent-Id') || undefined
    const access = checkTeamAccess({ teamId: id, requestingAgentId: agentId })
    if (!access.allowed) {
      return NextResponse.json({ error: access.reason }, { status: 403 })
    }
    const deleted = await deleteTeam(id)
    if (!deleted) {
      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Team not found' }, { status: 404 })
    }
    return NextResponse.json({ success: true })
  } catch (error) {
    console.error('[teams] DELETE error:', error)
    return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Internal server error' }, { status: 500 })
  }
}
```

     1→import { NextRequest, NextResponse } from 'next/server'  
     2→import { loadGovernance, setPassword, verifyPassword } from '@/lib/governance'  
     3→  
     4→export async function POST(request: NextRequest) {  
     5→  try {  
     6→    const body = await request.json()  
     7→    const { password, currentPassword } = body  
     8→  
     9→    if (!password || typeof password !== 'string' || password.length < 6) {  
    10→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Password must be at least 6 characters' }, { status: 400 })  
    11→    }  
    12→  
    13→    const config = loadGovernance()  
    14→  
    15→    // If password already set, require current password  
    16→    if (config.passwordHash) {  
    17→      if (!currentPassword || !verifyPassword(currentPassword)) {  
    18→        return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Invalid current password' }, { status: 401 })  
    19→      }  
    20→    }  
    21→  
    22→    await setPassword(password)  
    23→    return NextResponse.json({ success: true })  
    24→  } catch (error) {  
    25→    console.error('Failed to set password:', error)  
    26→    return NextResponse.json(  
    27→      { error: error instanceof Error ? error.message : 'Failed to set password' },  
    28→      { status: 500 }  
    29→    )  
    30→  }  
    31→}

     1→import { NextRequest, NextResponse } from 'next/server'  
     2→import { loadGovernance, setPassword, verifyPassword } from '@/lib/governance'  
     3→  
     4→export async function POST(request: NextRequest) {  
     5→  try {  
     6→    const body = await request.json()  
     7→    const { password, currentPassword } = body  
     8→  
     9→    if (!password || typeof password !== 'string' || password.length < 6) {  
    10→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Password must be at least 6 characters' }, { status: 400 })  
    11→    }  
    12→  
    13→    const config = loadGovernance()  
    14→  
    15→    // If password already set, require current password  
    16→    if (config.passwordHash) {  
    17→      if (!currentPassword || !verifyPassword(currentPassword)) {  
    18→        return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Invalid current password' }, { status: 401 })  
    19→      }  
    20→    }  
    21→  
    22→    const isChange = !!config.passwordHash  
    23→    await setPassword(password)  
    24→  
    25→    if (isChange) {  
    26→      console.log('[governance] Password changed at', new Date().toISOString())  
    27→    } else {  
    28→      console.log('[governance] Password set at', new Date().toISOString())  
    29→    }  
    30→  
    31→    return NextResponse.json({ success: true })  
    32→  } catch (error) {  
    33→    console.error('Failed to set password:', error)  
    34→    return NextResponse.json(  
    35→      { error: error instanceof Error ? error.message : 'Failed to set password' },  
    36→      { status: 500 }  
    37→    )  
    38→  }

     1→import { NextRequest, NextResponse } from 'next/server'  
     2→import { checkMessageAllowed } from '@/lib/message-filter'  
     3→import { loadAgents } from '@/lib/agent-registry'  
     4→  
     5→// In-memory cache: avoids re-reading governance + teams files for every agent  
     6→// on each request. TTL of 5 seconds balances freshness with performance.  
     7→const cache = new Map<string, { ids: string[]; expiresAt: number }>()  
     8→const CACHE_TTL_MS = 5_000  
     9→  
    10→export async function GET(request: NextRequest) {  
    11→  try {  
    12→    const agentId = request.nextUrl.searchParams.get('agentId')  
    13→  
    14→    if (!agentId) {  
    15→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'agentId query parameter is required' }, { status: 400 })  
    16→    }  
    17→  
    18→    // Check cache first  
    19→    const cached = cache.get(agentId)  
    20→    if (cached && Date.now() < cached.expiresAt) {  
    21→      return NextResponse.json({ reachableAgentIds: cached.ids })  
    22→    }  
    23→  
    24→    // Cache miss or expired — compute reachable agents  
    25→    const allAgents = loadAgents()  
    26→    const reachableAgentIds: string[] = []  
    27→  
    28→    for (const agent of allAgents) {  
    29→      if (agent.id === agentId) continue  
    30→      if (agent.deletedAt) continue  
    31→  
    32→      const result = checkMessageAllowed({  
    33→        senderAgentId: agentId,  
    34→        recipientAgentId: agent.id,  
    35→      })  
    36→  
    37→      if (result.allowed) {  
    38→        reachableAgentIds.push(agent.id)  
    39→      }  
    40→    }  
    41→  
    42→    // Store in cache with TTL  
    43→    cache.set(agentId, { ids: reachableAgentIds, expiresAt: Date.now() + CACHE_TTL_MS })  
    44→  
    45→    // Evict stale entries to prevent unbounded growth  
    46→    if (cache.size > 200) {  
    47→      const now = Date.now()  
    48→      for (const [key, entry] of cache) {  
    49→        if (now >= entry.expiresAt) cache.delete(key)  
    50→      }

     1→/**  
     2→ * Message Filter — enforces closed-team messaging isolation  
     3→ *  
     4→ * Determines whether a message from sender to recipient is allowed  
     5→ * based on governance roles (MANAGER, Chief-of-Staff) and closed-team  
     6→ * membership. Open-world agents (not in any closed team) can message  
     7→ * freely unless the recipient is inside a closed team.

    14→  recipientAgentId: string

    16→}  
    17→  
    18→export interface MessageFilterResult {  
    19→  allowed: boolean  
    20→  reason?: string  
    21→}  
    22→  
    23→/**  
    24→ * Check whether a message from sender to recipient is allowed.  
    25→ *  
    26→ * Algorithm (R6.1–R6.7):  
    27→ * 1. Mesh-forwarded (senderAgentId null): always allowed (trust mesh peers)  
    28→ * 2. Neither in a closed team: allowed (open world, current behavior) (R6.4)  
    29→ * 3. Sender is MANAGER: always allowed (R6.3)  
    30→ * 4. Sender is COS of any closed team: can reach MANAGER, other COS, own team members (R6.2)  
    31→ * 5. Normal closed-team member: can reach same-team members and own COS (R6.1)  
    32→ * 6. Outside sender to closed-team recipient: denied (R6.5)  
    33→ * 7. Default: allowed  
    34→ *  
    35→ * IMPORTANT (R6.7): Uses getClosedTeamsForAgent (plural) to correctly handle  
    36→ * COS agents who belong to multiple closed teams simultaneously.  
    37→ */

**Old:**  
```
export function checkMessageAllowed(input: MessageFilterInput): MessageFilterResult {
  const { senderAgentId, recipientAgentId } = input

  // Step 1: Mesh-forwarded messages are always trusted
  if (senderAgentId === null) {
    return { allowed: true }
  }

  // Load team membership for both parties — use plural to handle COS in multiple teams (R6.7)
  const senderTeams = getClosedTeamsForAgent(senderAgentId)
  const recipientTeams = getClosedTeamsForAgent(recipientAgentId)
  const senderInClosed = senderTeams.length > 0
  const recipientInClosed = recipientTeams.length > 0

  // Step 2: Neither party is in a closed team — open world, allow freely (R6.4)
  if (!senderInClosed && !recipientInClosed) {
    return { allowed: true }
  }

  // Step 3: MANAGER can message anyone (R6.3)
  if (isManager(senderAgentId)) {
    return { allowed: true }
  }

  // Step 4: Sender is Chief-of-Staff of some closed team (R6.2)
  if (isChiefOfStaffAnywhere(senderAgentId)) {
    // COS can always reach the MANAGER
    if (isManager(recipientAgentId)) {
      return { allowed: true }
    }
    // COS-to-COS bridge: any COS can message any other COS
    if (isChiefOfStaffAnywhere(recipientAgentId)) {
      return { allowed: true }
    }
    // COS can message members of ANY of their closed teams (R6.7 — plural, not singular)
    if (senderTeams.some(team => team.agentIds.includes(recipientAgentId))) {
      return { allowed: true }
    }
    return {
      allowed: false,
      reason: 'Chief-of-Staff can only message MANAGER, other Chiefs-of-Staff, and own team members',
    }
  }

  // Step 5: Sender is a normal member of a closed team (R6.1)
  if (senderInClosed) {
    // Can message members of the same closed team
    const shareTeam = senderTeams.some(team =>
      recipientTeams.some(rt => rt.id === team.id)
    )
    if (shareTeam) {
      return { allowed: true }
    }
    // Can message the COS

... [3606 more chars truncated]

**Result:**

The file /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/message-filter.ts has been updated successfully.

function tasksFilePath(teamId: string): string {
  // Validate teamId is a proper UUID to prevent path traversal attacks

  // Defense-in-depth: use basename to strip any directory components

}

     1→#!/bin/bash  
     2→# AI Maestro - Version Bump Script  
     3→# Centralizes version management across all files  
     4→#  
     5→# Usage:  
     6→#   ./scripts/bump-version.sh patch    # 0.17.12 -> 0.17.13  
     7→#   ./scripts/bump-version.sh minor    # 0.17.12 -> 0.18.0  
     8→#   ./scripts/bump-version.sh major    # 0.17.12 -> 1.0.0  
     9→#   ./scripts/bump-version.sh 0.18.0   # Set specific version  
    10→  
    11→set -e  
    12→  
    13→# Colors  
    14→RED='\033[0;31m'  
    15→GREEN='\033[0;32m'  
    16→YELLOW='\033[1;33m'  
    17→CYAN='\033[0;36m'  
    18→NC='\033[0m'  
    19→  
    20→# Get script directory and project root  
    21→SCRIPT_DIR="$(cd "$(dirname "${BASH_SOURCE[0]}")" && pwd)"  
    22→PROJECT_ROOT="$(dirname "$SCRIPT_DIR")"  
    23→  
    24→# Read current version from version.json  
    25→VERSION_FILE="$PROJECT_ROOT/version.json"  
    26→if [ ! -f "$VERSION_FILE" ]; then  
    27→    echo -e "${RED}Error: version.json not found${NC}"  
    28→    exit 1  
    29→fi  
    30→  
    31→CURRENT_VERSION=$(grep -o '"version": *"[^"]*"' "$VERSION_FILE" | cut -d'"' -f4)  
    32→echo -e "${CYAN}Current version: ${CURRENT_VERSION}${NC}"  
    33→  
    34→# Parse current version  
    35→IFS='.' read -r MAJOR MINOR PATCH <<< "$CURRENT_VERSION"  
    36→  
    37→# Determine new version  
    38→case "$1" in  
    39→    patch)  
    40→        PATCH=$((PATCH + 1))  
    41→        NEW_VERSION="${MAJOR}.${MINOR}.${PATCH}"  
    42→        ;;  
    43→    minor)  
    44→        MINOR=$((MINOR + 1))  
    45→        PATCH=0  
    46→        NEW_VERSION="${MAJOR}.${MINOR}.${PATCH}"  
    47→        ;;  
    48→    major)  
    49→        MAJOR=$((MAJOR + 1))  
    50→        MINOR=0  
    51→        PATCH=0  
    52→        NEW_VERSION="${MAJOR}.${MINOR}.${PATCH}"  
    53→        ;;  
    54→    "")  
    55→        echo ""  
    56→        echo "Usage: $0 <patch|minor|major|version>"  
    57→        echo ""  
    58→        echo "Examples:"  
    59→        echo "  $0 patch    # ${CURRENT_VERSION} -> ${MAJOR}.${MINOR}.$((PATCH + 1  

... [4706 more chars truncated]

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-16 21:13:52]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Wait -- the `update_file` function uses `grep -q "$pattern"` for detection and `sed` for replacement. Using regex like `[A-Za-z]* [0-9]*` will work in sed, but `grep -q` with that pattern should also work since grep supports basic regex. However, the `|` delimiter in the sed command inside `update_file` means my `\/` escaping for `/` in `</strong>` is correct for sed but the grep check might have issues with the escaped slashes. Let me re-examine the function.  

</div>

   100→update_file() {  
   101→    local file="$1"  
   102→    local pattern="$2"  
   103→    local replacement="$3"  
   104→    local description="$4"  
   105→  
   106→    if [ -f "$file" ]; then  
   107→        if grep -q "$pattern" "$file" 2>/dev/null; then  
   108→            _sed_inplace "$file" "s|$pattern|$replacement|g"  
   109→            echo -e "  ${GREEN}✓${NC} $description"  
   110→            FILES_UPDATED=$((FILES_UPDATED + 1))  
   111→        fi  
   112→    fi

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-16 21:14:04]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

The issue: `grep -q` is called with the same pattern that's used in `sed`. The pattern `<strong>Version:<\/strong>` has `\/` which is a sed escape for `/` inside `/pattern/replacement/` delimiters, but since this script uses `|` as the sed delimiter, the `\/` is unnecessary. More importantly, `grep` will interpret `\/` literally as `\/` which won't match the HTML.  

I need to rethink. The existing `update_file` calls use literal strings (no regex), so the same string works for both `grep` and `sed`. But I need regex for the month/year part.  

A better approach: use a fixed literal pattern for the grep check (just the version number part), and a regex pattern for the sed replacement. But `update_file` uses the same pattern for both. So I should either:  
1. Not use `update_file` and write custom logic (like item 8/BACKLOG.md does), or  
2. Use literal patterns that match exactly.  

Option 2 is tricky because I don't know the old month/year. But actually, I can compute the old month/year from the version.json's releaseDate or... Actually, the simplest approach is to just write custom sed commands like BACKLOG.md does.  

Let me rewrite the two entries to use direct sed instead of `update_file`.  

</div>

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-16 21:14:18]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Wait, there's another issue. The sed regex `([A-Za-z]* [0-9]*)` uses parentheses. In basic sed (default on macOS), parentheses are literal unless escaped with `\(` and `\)`. But here I don't need to capture -- I just need to match. The `(` and `)` in the HTML are literal characters, and `[A-Za-z]* [0-9]*` is the regex for the month name and year inside those literal parens.  

Actually, looking at the actual HTML: `0.23.11 (February 2026)`. The parentheses are literal characters in the HTML. In sed with `|` delimiter, `(` and `)` are literal in basic regex mode. So `$CURRENT_VERSION ([A-Za-z]* [0-9]*)` should match `0.23.11 (February 2026)` correctly in basic sed -- the `(` matches literal `(`, `[A-Za-z]*` matches `February`, space matches space, `[0-9]*` matches `2026`, and `)` matches literal `)`.  

Let me verify this works by doing a dry run.  

</div>


</details>

    18→function ensureDir(): void {

    20→    mkdirSync(AI_MAESTRO_DIR, { recursive: true })  
    21→  }  
    22→}  
    23→  
    24→/** Load all transfer requests from disk */  
    25→export function loadTransfers(): TransferRequest[] {  
    26→  ensureDir()  
    27→  if (!existsSync(TRANSFERS_FILE)) {  
    28→    return []  
    29→  }  
    30→  try {  
    31→    const raw = readFileSync(TRANSFERS_FILE, 'utf-8')  
    32→    const data: TransfersFile = JSON.parse(raw)  
    33→    return data.requests || []  
    34→  } catch {  
    35→    return []  
    36→  }  
    37→}

    40→function saveTransfers(requests: TransferRequest[]): void {  
    41→  ensureDir()  
    42→  const data: TransfersFile = { version: 1, requests }  
    43→  writeFileSync(TRANSFERS_FILE, JSON.stringify(data, null, 2), 'utf-8')  
    44→}

   115→/** Clean up old resolved requests (older than 30 days) */  
   116→export async function cleanupOldTransfers(): Promise<number> {  
   117→  return withLock('transfers', () => {  
   118→    const requests = loadTransfers()  
   119→    const cutoff = new Date()  
   120→    cutoff.setDate(cutoff.getDate() - 30)  
   121→    const cutoffStr = cutoff.toISOString()  
   122→  
   123→    const filtered = requests.filter(r => {  
   124→      if (r.status === 'pending') return true // Keep all pending  
   125→      return (r.resolvedAt || r.createdAt) > cutoffStr  
   126→    })  
   127→  
   128→    const removed = requests.length - filtered.length  
   129→    if (removed > 0) saveTransfers(filtered)  
   130→    return removed  
   131→  })

   115→  
   116→// Exported for future scheduled cleanup integration  
   117→/** Clean up old resolved requests (older than 30 days) */  
   118→export async function cleanupOldTransfers(): Promise<number> {  
   119→  return withLock('transfers', () => {  
   120→    const requests = loadTransfers()  
   121→    const cutoff = new Date()  
   122→    cutoff.setDate(cutoff.getDate() - 30)  
   123→    const cutoffStr = cutoff.toISOString()  
   124→  
   125→    const filtered = requests.filter(r => {  
   126→      if (r.status === 'pending') return true // Keep all pending  
   127→      return (r.resolvedAt || r.createdAt) > cutoffStr  
   128→    })  
   129→  
   130→    const removed = requests.length - filtered.length  
   131→    if (removed > 0) saveTransfers(filtered)  
   132→    return removed  
   133→  })  
   134→}

**New:**  
```
  // Derive governance role from current state
  const agentRole: GovernanceRole = useMemo(() => {
    if (!agentId) return 'normal'
    if (managerId === agentId) return 'manager'
    // team.type is now required per types/team.ts
    const isCOS = allTeams.some(
      (t) => t.type === 'closed' && t.chiefOfStaffId === agentId
    )
    if (isCOS) return 'chief-of-staff'
    return 'normal'
  }, [agentId, managerId, allTeams])

  // Derive cosTeams: closed teams where this agent is chief-of-staff
  // team.type is now required per types/team.ts
  const cosTeams = useMemo(() => agentId
    ? allTeams.filter((t) => t.type === 'closed' && t.chiefOfStaffId === agentId)
    : [], [agentId, allTeams])

  // Derive memberTeams: teams where agentIds includes this agent
  const memberTeams = useMemo(() => agentId
    ? allTeams.filter((t) => t.agentIds.includes(agentId))
    : [], [agentId, allTeams])

   188→function ensureTeamsDir() {

   193→  
   194→export function loadTeams(): Team[] {  
   195→  try {  
   196→    ensureTeamsDir()  
   197→    if (!fs.existsSync(TEAMS_FILE)) {  
   198→      return []  
   199→    }  
   200→    const data = fs.readFileSync(TEAMS_FILE, 'utf-8')  
   201→    const parsed: TeamsFile = JSON.parse(data)  
   202→    const teams = Array.isArray(parsed.teams) ? parsed.teams : []  
   203→  
   204→    // Migration: ensure all teams have a type field (default to 'open')  
   205→    let needsSave = false  
   206→    for (const team of teams) {  
   207→      if (!team.type) {  
   208→        team.type = 'open'  
   209→        needsSave = true  
   210→      }  
   211→    }  
   212→    if (needsSave) {  
   213→      saveTeams(teams)  
   214→    }  
   215→  
   216→    return teams  
   217→  } catch (error) {  
   218→    console.error('Failed to load teams:', error)  
   219→    return []  
   220→  }  
   221→}  
   222→

   226→    const file: TeamsFile = { version: 1, teams }

   228→    return true  
   229→  } catch (error) {

Two MUST-FIX changes:  

1. **forwardFromUI bypass** (around line 360+): `forwardFromUI()` never calls `checkMessageAllowed()`. Add governance message filtering in forwardFromUI() AFTER resolving both the sender and recipient agents, using the same pattern as `sendFromUI()` (look at lines ~153-161 for the pattern). If the filter blocks the message, throw an Error with the filter's reason.  

2. **Unresolved recipient bypass** (around lines 145-161): When `toResolved.agentId` is `''` (falsy), the guard `if (fromAgent?.agentId && toResolved.agentId)` skips `checkMessageAllowed()`. Fix the guard:  
   - Change to only require `fromAgent?.agentId`   
   - For the recipient ID passed to checkMessageAllowed, use `toResolved.agentId || toResolved.alias || 'unknown'`  
   - This ensures messages from agents in closed teams are still filtered even when recipient is unresolved  

Make sure `checkMessageAllowed` is imported from `@/lib/message-filter` (or wherever it's defined).

     1→/**  
     2→ * Message Send - Web UI message composition + routing  
     3→ *  
     4→ * Replaces the write half of sendMessage() / forwardMessage() from messageQueue.ts.  
     5→ * Web UI endpoints (/api/messages POST, /api/agents/[id]/messages POST, etc.) call  
     6→ * sendFromUI() and forwardFromUI().  
     7→ *  
     8→ * Flow:  
     9→ *   1. Resolve sender/recipient agents  
    10→ *   2. Build AMP envelope + payload  
    11→ *   3. Apply content security  
    12→ *   4. Local → deliver(), Remote → HTTP forward, External+offline → relay queue  
    13→ *   5. Write sender's sent folder  
    14→ *   6. Return Message object for response compatibility  
    15→ */

   128→export async function sendFromUI(options: SendFromUIOptions): Promise<{ message: Message; notified: boolean }> {  
   129→  const { from, to, subject, content } = options

     1→/**  
     2→ * File Lock — in-process mutex for serializing load→modify→save operations  
     3→ *  
     4→ * Prevents concurrent read-modify-write races within a single Node.js process.  
     5→ * Each registry file gets its own named lock. When one API request is mid-write,  
     6→ * other requests for the same file queue up and run sequentially.  
     7→ *  
     8→ * This is sufficient for Phase 1 (single Next.js process, localhost).  
     9→ * For multi-process deployments, replace with advisory file locks (e.g., proper-lockfile).  
    10→ */  
    11→  
    12→// Map of lock name -> queue of pending resolve callbacks  
    13→const locks = new Map<string, Array<() => void>>()  
    14→// Set of currently held lock names  
    15→const held = new Set<string>()  
    16→  
    17→/**  
    18→ * Acquire a named lock. Returns a release function.  
    19→ * If the lock is already held, the caller awaits until it is released.  
    20→ */  
    21→export function acquireLock(name: string): Promise<() => void> {  
    22→  if (!held.has(name)) {  
    23→    // Lock is free — acquire immediately  
    24→    held.add(name)  
    25→    return Promise.resolve(() => releaseLock(name))  
    26→  }  
    27→  
    28→  // Lock is held — enqueue and wait  
    29→  return new Promise<() => void>((resolve) => {  
    30→    if (!locks.has(name)) {

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-16 21:11:03]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Read -- `file-lock.ts`</summary>

**Input:**

{
  "file_path": "/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/file-lock.ts",

**Result:**

    20→ */  
    21→export function acquireLock(name: string): Promise<() => void> {  
    22→  if (!held.has(name)) {  
    23→    // Lock is free — acquire immediately  
    24→    held.add(name)  
    25→    return Promise.resolve(() => releaseLock(name))  
    26→  }  
    27→  
    28→  // Lock is held — enqueue and wait  
    29→  return new Promise<() => void>((resolve) => {  
    30→    if (!locks.has(name)) {  
    31→      locks.set(name, [])  
    32→    }  
    33→    locks.get(name)!.push(() => {  
    34→      resolve(() => releaseLock(name))  
    35→    })  
    36→  })  
    37→}  
    38→  
    39→/**  
    40→ * Release a named lock and wake the next waiter if any.  
    41→ */  
    42→function releaseLock(name: string): void {  
    43→  const queue = locks.get(name)  
    44→  if (queue && queue.length > 0) {  
    45→    // Hand lock to next waiter (don't remove from held set)  
    46→    const next = queue.shift()!  
    47→    if (queue.length === 0) {  
    48→      locks.delete(name)  
    49→    }  
    50→    next()  
    51→  } else {  
    52→    // No waiters — release the lock  
    53→    held.delete(name)  
    54→    locks.delete(name)  
    55→  }  
    56→}  
    57→  
    58→/**  
    59→ * Run a function under a named lock.  
    60→ * Convenience wrapper: acquires, runs fn, releases (even on error).  
    61→ */  
    62→export async function withLock<T>(name: string, fn: () => T | Promise<T>): Promise<T> {  
    63→  const release = await acquireLock(name)  
    64→  try {  
    65→    return await fn()  
    66→  } finally {  
    67→    release()  
    68→  }  
    69→}  

</details>


## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-16 21:11:12]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

The lock is NOT reentrant - calling `withLock('teams', ...)` while already holding 'teams' would deadlock. So I cannot just wrap the whole block in `withLock` and still call `updateTeam` (which also uses `withLock('teams', ...)`).  

The correct fix is to use `acquireLock`/`releaseLock` pattern manually, or better: use `loadTeams()` inside the lock and do the save directly instead of calling `updateTeam`. But that would be a bigger refactor.   

The simplest correct approach: use `acquireLock` directly, then call `loadTeams()` inside the lock, and instead of calling `updateTeam` (which would deadlock), do the team modifications and save directly. But that duplicates the validation logic in `updateTeam`.  

Actually, the better approach is to use `acquireLock` explicitly at the top, and replace the `updateTeam` calls with direct `saveTeams` calls within the same lock. Let me check if `saveTeams` is exported.

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-16 21:12:16]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Wait -- there's a subtle issue. On line 130, `fromTeam.name` is accessed after the `finally` block releases the lock. At that point `fromTeam` was declared with `let` and assigned inside the try block, but if we returned early (e.g., fromTeam not found), we'd never reach line 130. The issue is that `fromTeam` could technically be `undefined` at line 130 since it's typed as `... | undefined`. TypeScript won't know it's guaranteed to be set after the try/finally. Let me check: if we reach line 123, that means we did NOT return early inside the try block, so `fromTeam` IS defined. But TypeScript doesn't narrow that. We need a `!` assertion or a guard.  

Actually, looking again at lines 130-131, `fromTeam.name` would be a TypeScript error because `fromTeam` is typed as `... | undefined`. Let me add a safety guard:  

</div>

    24→      await removeManager()

    32→    // Verify agent exists  
    33→    const agent = getAgent(agentId)  
    34→    if (!agent) {  
    35→      return NextResponse.json({ error: `Agent '${agentId}' not found` }, { status: 404 })  
    36→    }  
    37→  
    38→    await setManager(agentId)

   124→    const fetchRepos = async () => {  
   125→      setLoadingRepos(true)  
   126→      try {  
   127→        const response = await fetch(`${baseUrl}/api/agents/${agentId}/repos`)  
   128→        if (response.ok) {  
   129→          const data = await response.json()  
   130→          setRepositories(data.repositories || [])  
   131→          setReposLoaded(true)  
   132→        }  
   133→      } catch (error) {  
   134→        console.error('Failed to fetch repos:', error)  
   135→      } finally {  
   136→        setLoadingRepos(false)  
   137→      }  
   138→    }  
   139→  
   140→    fetchRepos()  
   141→  }, [isOpen, agentId, expandedSections.repositories, reposLoaded, baseUrl])  
   142→  
   143→  // Fetch used avatars (all avatars from other agents on this host)  

</details>


## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-16 21:13:49]*
